Notice 
This guide is the second and updated version of "Improved Hot Mix Asphalt Design Manual 
(Superpave System - Marshall Method)” Issued in Muharram 1442 H corresponding to 
August 2020, and the updates within this version included the following: 
•
Update the name "Ministry of Transport and its acronym MOT" to "Ministry of Transport and 
Logistic Services and its acronym MOTLS". 
•
Update the name of the "Innovation, Quality and Environment Center" to the "General 
Department of Quality and Environment".  
•
Update the Ministry's logo to the new logo (Ministry of Transport and Logistic Services). 
•
Update definition of Gmm, Gmb and MOT under (Definitions and Abbreviations) section. 
•
Adding the moisture of (RAP) to the design of the hot mix asphalt (with the addition of RAP), 
paragraphs (3.1.1 - c) and (3.2.1 - c).

Introduction by His Excellency Eng. Saleh Al-Jasser 
The Minister of Transport and Logistic Services 
 
The growth and development in the road network are a 
true indication of the generous support of the government 
of his Highness, Custodian of the Two Holy Mosques, King 
Salman bin Abdulaziz, and the insightful vision of his 
Highness Crown Prince Mohammed bin Salman, as well 
as the effort exerted by the Ministry of Transport and 
Logistics Services and its representatives. Where the 
road sector is among the most essential components of 
the infrastructure and considered as a measure of development due to the 
continuing benefits that relate to the mobility of people, transferring of goods, raw 
materials, and communications between interrelated regions and cities alike. 
 
As the road sector in the Kingdom witnessed a noticeable development during the 
past decades, the Ministry of Transport and Logistics Services served to plan, 
design, and construct a wide network of high-performance sustainable roads in 
cooperation with established partners ranging from private companies and 
consulting offices. The Ministry has developed mechanisms and models that 
assist in designing hot asphalt mixtures such as Marshall – Superpave methods, 
to be enforced on road and bridge projects corresponding with sustainable and 
international best practices and standard specifications. Appreciations are 
addressed to everyone who contributed in preparing this established guide in 
internalizing external costs and enhancing road safety. 
 
Finally, we ask God to grant prosperity to the Ministry's representatives. 
 
Introduction by His Excellency Eng. Saleh Al-Jasser

A Word by Eng/ Badir bin Abdullah Al-Dalami 
The Vice Minister for Roads Affairs 
The road network in the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia is the 
latest and most developed in the region and for this, the 
Ministry has paid attention to improving this network and 
maintaining 
its 
performance 
within 
international 
standards to keep pace with modern requirements and 
to maintain its distinguished position in this field. 
The Ministry has set multiple goals that involve raising 
the performance efficiency and enhancing quality 
standards in accordance with the best international practice. The Ministry’s 
concern to preserve the environment and reduce the costs of construction and 
maintenance of roads. It has developed this comprehensive guide to be the 
reference in design of hot asphalt mixtures (Marshall - Superpave) methods with 
the addition of the ability to use reclaimed asphalt within asphalt mix complying 
with international standards and specifications in road and bridge projects. 
Furthermore, this guide is an important step towards achieving the Kingdom’s 
Vision 2030 followed by the vision of the Ministry of Transport and the 
achievement various benefits such as rationalization of consumption in road 
construction materials and reduce the costs of construction and maintenance 
plus the permanent pursuit to preserve the environment from pollution, which 
occurs from reclaimed asphalt of roads within the maintenance activity. 
The design methods verification within this guide are based on fundamentals and 
standards that mimic local and international experiences, including implementing 
uniform standards within design methods, using reclaimed asphalt, and 
mechanisms for enhancing the asphalt binder in proportion to the capabilities of 
companies, factories and consulting offices - validating designs for hot asphalt 
mixtures (Superpave / Marshall) - Analysis and research of data, results, and 
documentation - The Ministry’s specialists verify the submitted data, collect 
samples, verify conformity and grant approvals for designs that meet the 
requirements. Finally, I would like to thank everyone who contributed to preparing 
this guide. 
And I ask God for success for all.

Definitions and Abbreviations 
AASHTO 
American Association of State Highway and Transportation Officials 
ASTM 
American Society for Testing and Materials 
Abson 
Method 
A method used for recovery of asphalt binder from solvent 
AV 
Air Voids in Compacted Mixture – The small air spaces between the 
asphalt binder coated aggregate particles in the compacted asphalt 
mixture 
BBR 
Bending Beam Rheometer – A device for measuring the low temperature 
stiffness of asphalt binder 
CAA 
Coarse Aggregate Angularity test - a method of determining the 
angularity of coarse aggregate. Coarse aggregate angularity is 
important to ensure adequate aggregate interlock and prevent 
excessive HMA deformation under load 
DAS   
Design Aggregate Structure – The aggregate blend that meets the 
Superpave requirements 
DAC 
Design Asphalt Content – The percentage of asphalt binder at 4.0% of air 
voids in the selected mix that meets the Superpave requirements 
DSR 
Dynamic Shear Rheometer – A device to measure the shear modulus 
and phase angle of asphalt binder at different temperatures and loading 
frequencies 
DP 
Dust Proportion – The proportion of the percentage by mass of the 
material passing the 0.075mm sieve to the effective binder content by 
mass of the mix in percent 
ESAL 
Equivalent Single Axle Load – The number of applications of the 
standard axle that is equivalent in the damage to the pavement to an axle 
of any mass 
FAA 
Fine Aggregate Angularity test - an indirect method of assessing the 
angularity of fine aggregate. Fine aggregate angularity is important 
because an excess of rounded fine aggregate can lead to HMA rutting 
F&E 
Flat- and-Elongated Particles test - used to determine the dimensional 
ratios for aggregate particles of specific sieve sizes 
Gb 
Specific Gravity of Asphalt Binder – The ratio of the mass in air of a unit 
volume of an asphalt binder at a stated temperature to the mass in air 
of an equal volume of gas-free distilled water at the same temperature 
 
 
Definitions and Abbreviations
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
                                    
                           Page 9 of 69  
Improved Hot Mix 
Asphalt Design Manual  
Kingdom of Saudi Arabia 
Ministry of Transport           
and Logistics Services 
Roads Construction Deputyship 
General Department of Quality 
and Environment  
Gb(RAP) 
Specific Gravity of the RAP Asphalt Binder – The ratio of the mass in air 
of a unit volume of the RAP asphalt binder at a stated temperature to the 
mass in air of an equal volume of gas-free distilled water at the same 
temperature 
Gmb 
Bulk Specific Gravity of Compacted Mixture - The ratio of the mass in air 
of a unit volume of a compacted specimen of an asphalt mixture 
Including the permeable and impermeable spaces attached to the 
surface of the sample at a stated temperature to the mass in air of an 
equal volume of gas-free distilled water at the same temperature. 
Gmm 
Maximum Specific Gravity of Bituminous Mixture – The ratio of the mass 
in air of a unit volume of uncompacted or loose asphalt mixture without 
air spaces at a stated temperature to the mass in air of an equal volume 
of gas-free distilled water at the same temperature 
Gmm(RAP) 
Maximum Specific Gravity of the RAP – The ratio of the mass in air of a 
unit volume of the loose RAP at stated temperature to the mass in air of 
an equal volume of gas-free distilled water at the same temperature 
Gn 
Bulk or Apparent Specific Gravities of Aggregates 
Gsa 
Apparent Specific Gravity of Aggregate – The ratio of the mass in air of 
unit volume of an impermeable aggregate or stone at stated 
temperature to the mass in air of an equal volume of gas-free distilled 
water at the same temperature 
Gsb 
Bulk Specific Gravity of Aggregate – The ratio of the mass in air of unit 
volume of a permeable (including both permeable and impermeable 
voids) aggregate at stated temperature to the mass in air of an equal 
volume of gas-free distilled water at the same temperature 
Gsb(RAP,agg) 
RAP Aggregate Bulk Specific Gravity – The Bulk Specific Gravity of RAP 
aggregate cannot be measured directly, it’s necessary to estimate it 
Gse 
Effective Specific Gravity of Aggregate – The ratio of the mass in air of 
unit volume of a permeable (excluding voids permeable to the asphalt 
binder) aggregate at stated temperature to the mass in air of an equal 
volume of gas-free distilled water at the same temperature 
Gse(RAP,agg) 
RAP Aggregate Effective Specific Gravity   
HMA 
Hot Mix Asphalt – A mixture of aggregate and asphalt binder produced 
at temperature above 135 ℃ 
JMF 
Job Mix Formula – The end result of a successful mix design of a 
recommended mixture of aggregate and asphalt binder 
MOT 
Ministry of Transport 
MRDTM 
Materials and Research Department Test Method

Multiple Stress Creep Recovery – A test to determine the elastic behavior 
of asphalt binder 
Mdryrap 
Mass of dry RAP in grams 
MRAPAgg 
Mass of RAP aggregate in grams 
MSDS 
Supply Materials Safety Data Sheet 
NMS 
Nominal Maximum Size of Aggregate – One standard size larger than the 
first sieve to remain more than 10 percent of aggregate 
Ninitial 
Initial Number of Gyrations – Number of gyrations of the gyratory 
compactor simulating the construction traffic 
Ndesign 
Design Number of Gyrations – Number of gyrations of the gyratory 
compactor simulating the design traffic 
Nmaximum 
Maximum Number of Gyrations – Number of gyrations of the gyratory 
compactor simulating the highest traffic 
OPC 
One-point check – A procedure by the Ministry of Transport done in the 
laboratory to ensure that the materials used by contractor in the asphalt 
mixture are in accordance with the specifications and also to ensure that 
the hot asphalt mixture conforms to the specifications in order to verify 
the design before production 
PG 
Performance Graded – The Superpave binder specifications are 
performance-based; 
therefore, 
these 
binders 
are 
known 
as 
performance-graded binders 
PCS 
Primary Control Sieve – The sieve that is used to separate the coarse 
and fine aggregate and it is based on the Nominal Maximum Particle Size 
of the aggregate blend 
PAV 
Pressure Aging Vessel – A device for rapidly oxidizing asphalt binder in 
laboratory to simulate approximately 5 years of filed aging 
Ps 
Percentage of Aggregate in the mixture 
Pb 
Percentage of Binder in the mixture 
Pb(RAP) 
Percentage of Asphalt Binder content in the RAP 
Pba(RAP,agg) 
Asphalt Binder Absorption of the RAP aggregate 
Pbe 
Effective PG Binder Content – The total asphalt binder content minus the 
amount of asphalt binder that is absorbed into the aggregate particles 
or it’s the amount of asphalt binder that remains as the coating of the 
aggregate particles 
Pn 
% of individual aggregate components, based on total mass of aggregate 
mixture 
RTFO 
Rolling Thin Film Oven – A device for oxidizing asphalt binder in 
laboratory to simulate the asphalt plant aging

RAP 
Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement – Asphalt paving material milled or 
scraped off an existing bituminous pavement, consisting of aggregate 
and asphalt binder 
SASO 
Saudi Arabian Standards Organization 
SE 
Sand Equivalent test – a test to show the relative proportions of fine dust 
or clay-like materials in fine aggregate 
SP 
Softening Point – The temperature at which an asphalt binder sample 
can no longer support the weight of a 3.5-g steel ball 
TSR 
Tensile Strength Ratio – The wet conditioned (treatment group) indirect 
tensile strength divided by the dry (control group) indirect tensile 
strength 
VMA 
Voids in the Mineral Aggregate – The intergranular void space between 
the aggregate particles of a compacted paving mixture that includes the 
air voids and the effective asphalt content, expressed as a percent of the 
total volume 
VFA 
Voids Filled with Asphalt – The percentage of VMA filled with asphalt 
binder

1 Introduction 
 
This manual describes the methodology for developing and reviewing hot mix asphalt 
mixture designs. Its summaries the complete Hot Mix Asphalt (HMA) design procedures 
using: 
• Superpave System 
• Marshall Method  
 
The goal of the HMA design is to determine an economical blend of PG asphalt binder 
and aggregate producing a paving mixture with sufficient Air Voids (AV), Voids in the 
Mineral Aggregate (VMA) and Voids Filled with Asphalt (VFA) that will perform 
adequately over the pavement’s service life. The mixture and asphalt binder 
requirements are developed to suit the climate and traffic conditions that pavements are 
exposed to at projects sites across the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia (KSA). The most current 
version of Ministry of Transport (MOT), American Association of State Highway and 
Transportation Officials (AASHTO), and American Society for Testing and Materials 
(ASTM) are being used including:  
 
Table 1. Standard Test Procedures

HMA Producer shall furnish a complete HMA design. HMA design shall be submitted for 
approval at least 30 days before production. Ministry of Transport (MOT) may collect 
HMA samples along with random samples from HMA ingredients as needed to review 
the HMA design for approval. Details of HMA designs methods are next.

2 HMA Design (Virgin)  
 
The virgin HMA is defined as the mixture that include only virgin materials (aggregate 
and asphalt). Details for virgin HMA design using both systems (Superpave and Marshall) 
are given next. 
 
 
2.1 
Superpave System using new material (Virgin) 
2.1.1 Design steps for Superpave system (Virgin) 
HMA design and Job Mix Formula (JMF) development involves the following steps: 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Material Selection 
1 
Design Aggregate 
Structure (DAS) 
2 
Design Asphalt 
Content (DAC) 
3 
Moisture Susceptibility 
Evaluation 
4 
Rutting Resistance 
Evaluation
 
5

2-HMA Design (virgin)

General Department of Quality 
and Environment  
 
The selection step includes the following:  
Bitumen class: These values can be obtained from the temperature-zoning map of 
the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia (Figure 1). The PG binder (PG XXZ-YY) is denoted by 
performance grade using the multiple stress creep recovery (MSCR) test. The XX 
value refers to the average 7-day maximum pavement design temperature and 
the  -YY value to minimum pavement design temperature for one day in a year 
within 20 years in row. The Z value depends on the traffic loading, speed and refers 
to the Binder Class Designation (Table 2). 
 
Aggregate: Aggregates shall meet the requirements of MOT Source properties 
Specifications such as toughness, soundness, clay lumps & friable particles and 
specific consensus characteristics as shown in table 3.  e.g. for coarse aggregate 
angularity (CCA), fine aggregate angularity (FAA), flat- and-elongated particles 
(F&E), and sand equivalent (SE). The aggregate consensus property requirements 
are based on estimated traffic volume

The characteristics of the aggregate are determined based on the expected traffic on the 
project and the depth of the layer location (i.e. the distance from the road surface in 
millimeters) to the surface of the layer to be designed the mixture for, and in order for 
the aggregates to be used in SuperPave mixtures, these aggregates must match two 
sets of requirements known as the source properties and consensus properties. The 
requirements for the source properties are not specified in the SuperPave system, but 
the Ministry has the right to specify what it deems appropriate. As for the requirements 
for consensus properties, they are mentioned as shown in Table (3). 
 
It is recommended that at least three trial aggregate blend gradations are blended. This 
section describes the aggregate blend requirements and procedure to determine the

aggregate for each blend should meet the aggregate consensus properties (Table 3)  
The combined aggregate for each aggregate blend should have a Nominal Maximum Size 
(NMS) that does not exceed ½ to ⅓ the layer thickness. Mixtures with NMS of 4.75, 9.5, 
12.5 and 19.0 mm shall be used for HMA surface courses, while mixtures with NMS of 
25.0 and 37.5 mm shall be used for HMA base courses, unless otherwise specified in the 
Contracts Documents. Details of aggregate properties are next.

deep from the road surface and the second one is more than 100 mm deep. If more than 25% 
of the layer to be designed falls in the first section then the layer can be considered in the 
first section for the design purposes and if less than 25% of the layer falls in the first section 
then the layer can be considered in the second section

4. PCS Control Points. All other gradations shall be classified as fine graded.

gyrations, and another two to determine maximum specific gravity. Estimate the 
volumetric properties at 4.0% air voids for each blend. Compare the estimated 
volumetric properties from each blend with design criteria, Table 6, and choose one 
blend that best satisfies the volumetric criteria.  
 
 
 
From the estimated binder content of the previous step, determine 4 binder contents. 
These 4 binder contents are the estimated binder content, ± 0.5% of the estimated 
content and +1.0% of the estimated content as follows: 
1. Prepare two samples with the selected design aggregate structure for each 
percentage using the gyratory compactor and compact to Ndes gyrations; in 
addition, prepare two other samples to test the theoretical maximum specific 
gravity (Gmm) 
2. Perform a volumetric analysis of the samples to calculate air voids %AV, 
percentage of voids in mineral aggregate %VMA, percentage of voids filled with 
asphalt % VFA and percent of maximum specific gravity % (Gmm) at Ninitial. 
3. Draw the design curves between the binder content and each of  (Air voids (AV%), 
- Void in mineral aggregate  (VMA%) - the percent maximum specific gravity 
“%Gmm” at Ninitial - voids filled with asphalt % VFA.) 
4. From the curves, define the design asphalt content as the asphalt content that 
achieve a percentage of air voids equal to 4%. 
5. Verify that all design requirements are fulfilled at the design content of the asphalt 
binder, shown in Table 6. If any of the design requirements are not met at the 
selected design PG binder content, modify the design aggregate structure. 
 
After ensuring that all the design requirements are met for the design asphalt content, 
it must be ensured that the asphalt mixture meets the design requirements at the 
maximum number of gyrations (Nmax), as follows: 
1. Prepare at least two specimens with the selected design aggregate structure at 
the design PG binder content and compact the specimens to Nmax gyrations. 
2. Prepare two other samples to test the theoretical maximum specific gravity (Gmm) 
3. Determine the average %Gmm of the specimens and confirm that it satisfies the 
design requirement given in Table 6. If the requirement is not met at the design 
PG binder content, modify the design as needed. 
3. Design Asphalt Content (DAC)

The mixture is tested to assess its ability to resist moisture induce damage. Prepare at 
least six gyratory compacted specimens (150 mm diameters). Compact the specimens 
to 7 ± 0.5% of Air Voids and 95 ± 5 mm Height; The results of compacted Nmax samples 
can be used to determine the level of compaction required to obtain compacted samples, 
the percentage of air voids in it is within the required limits. After that the six (6) samples 
are divided into two subgroups, three of these samples are called the control group and 
placed in the air, while the remaining three samples are called the treatment group and 
placed in a water bath at a temperature of 60 ° C for 24 hours.  
Determine the Tensile Strength Ratio (TSR) of each specimen according to AASHTO T 
283. If the indirect tensile strength ratio is less than 80%, corrective action is required. 
When corrective action is necessary, any changes made to the design must be noted on 
the JMF, and all other volumetric and mechanical properties must be evaluated for 
compliance with requirements. Corrective action to improve the moisture susceptibility 
such as the use of anti-strip additives. Low test results for moisture sensitivity may 
indicate potential adhesion problems between the binder and aggregate or mix 
cohesiveness problems.  
 
 
The rut resistance is evaluated using the Hamburg Wheel Track test as per AASHTO T 
324. At least four gyratory compacted specimens (150 mm diameter), proportioned 
according to the JMF. Compact the specimens to 7 ± 0.5% of Air Voids. Determine the rut 
depth and the maximum number of passes to failure. The rut depth must not exceed 12.5 
mm  at the minimum number of cycles. The Hamburg Wheel tests requirements will 
depend on the PG Binder high temperature as shown in Table 7.  
Table 7 Hamburg Wheel Test Requirements 
High-Temperature Binder Grade 
Minimum No. of cycles @ 12.5 mm 
Ruth Depth, Tested @ 50°C 
PG 64 or lower 
10000 cycles 
PG 70 
15000 cycles 
PG 76 or higher 
20000 cycles 
Note: 1 cycle is equal to 2 passes

2.1.2 Superpave Specimen Formulation (Virgin) 
 
a. Aggregate Preparation 
Get representative aggregate samples as per AASHTO R 90. The sample shall be 
enough to prepare the required gyratory compacted specimens and specific gravity 
samples. Because additional tests are often required, it is recommended that 
additional aggregate components to be obtained when sampling. It is required that 
aggregate samples should be obtained from the individual hot bins. Prepare 
aggregate samples for the batching of gyratory compacted specimens and 
maximum specific gravity samples using aggregate size fractions in Table 8. 
The mixture samples are prepared according to the requirements of source and 
consensus characteristics as well as volumetric characteristics according to Table 
6 and the application of the Job Mix Formula (JMF) selected.

b. Determine mixing and compacting temperature 
The mixing and compaction temperatures are determined from the rotational 
viscosity test at the viscosity values (0.17 ± 0.02) and (0.28 ± 0.03) Pa, respectively, 
when performing the viscosity test according to the specifications of the American 
Association of State Highway Transportation Officials (AASHTO T 316) as follows: 
1. Determine rotational viscosity of the asphalt binder at 135°C and 165°C. 
2. Plot the rotational viscosity values at 135°C and 165°C on the Temperature-
Viscosity Relationship diagram then draw a line connecting these two points. 
3. The compaction temperature limits are the points of intersection of the line 
with the compaction range at the viscosity values (0.28 ± 0.03). 
4. The mixing temperature limits are the points of intersection of the line with 
the mixing range at the viscosity values (0.17 ± 0.02). 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Figure 2 Temperature – Viscosity Relationship

c. Specimen Batching and Compaction 
1. Batching   
Usually, a minimum of two gyratory compacted specimens and two mixture 
maximum specific gravity samples are prepared for each bitumen content. 
The gyratory specimens and mixture’s maximum specific gravity samples 
must be batched by aggregate component and size fraction. MOT 
recommends that the specimens be mixed individually to reduce the potential 
for error. Do not forget to add the minus No.200 size material to account. The 
required gyratory compacted specimen size is 115 mm ± 5 mm in height by 
150 mm in diameter. The maximum specific gravity sample size of the 
mixture varies depending on the nominal maximum aggregate size of the 
mixture being tested. The composition of each gyratory compacted specimen 
and mixture maximum specific gravity sample is determined according to the 
following procedure: 
 
a. Determine the specimen’s PG binder content. 
b. Estimate the weight of aggregate mass required to produce compacted 
specimen of the dimensions of 115 mm ± 5 mm in height by 150 mm in 
diameter. The mixture maximum specific gravity sample size is predetermined 
based on the nominal maximum aggregate size of the mixture. 
c. Determine the percentage of aggregate in the specimen from Equation 1.

g. Place the container in the oven and heat to the mixing temperature. Charge the 
mixing bowl with the heated aggregate and add the required amount of binder. 
At this point, the temperature of the aggregate and the asphalt must be within 
the limits of the mixing temperatures. Do not hold asphalt binder at mixing 
temperature more than one hour. 
h. Mix the aggregate and asphalt binder (preferably with a mechanical mixer) as 
quickly and thoroughly as possible to yield a mixture having a uniform 
distribution of asphalt. 
i. 
Place the mixture in the oven for two hours at compaction temperature.  
j.

1. The theoretical maximum specific gravity (Gmm) samples and 
allow it to cooldown at room temperature, taking into consideration 
its sensitivity. 
2. Sample each mold separately to be compacted upon the number of 
specific gyrations according to Table 10.  
 
 
2. Compaction 
Gyratory specimens will be compacted to the number of gyrations as shown 
in Table 10. The traffic level will be provided in the Contract Documents. 
Compaction is done as follows: 
a. After mixing the aggregate with the binder content, place the HMA samples in 
the oven and heat to compaction temperature for two hours. 
b. Put the gyratory mold and the base and top plate in oven at compaction 
temperature for two hours.  
c. After two hours, remove the mold and the plates from the oven, put the base 
plat in position in the mold, and place a paper disk on the plate. 
d.  Drop the mixture into the mold using a funnel or other device but take care to 
avoid segregation of the mix in the mold. Level the mix in the mold, place a paper 
disk and mold top plate. 
e. Place the mold in the gyratory compactor and compact to the required number 
of gyrations. 
f. After compaction, remove the base plate and the paper disks and allow the 
specimen to cool at room temperature.

For that aggregate blend, the producers can either use their experience with the 
materials or computational formula to determine estimated binder content. 
 
 
 
From the experimental content of the asphalt binder from the previous step, specify five 
percentages for the asphalt binder, which is the experimental content ± 0.5% and also ± 
1% and the experimental content itself is as follows: 
1. Prepare 3 samples for each percentage (3 molds x 5 asphalt ratios = 15 molds) in 
addition to three other samples to test the theoretical maximum specific density (Gmm) 
2. Test the stability, flow, and volumetric properties of the samples. 
3. Draw the design curves between the binder content and each of (Air voids (AV%), - 
Void in mineral aggregate (VMA%) - the maximum specific density “Gmm” - stability and 
flow.) 
4. From the curves, define the asphalt content as the average asphalt contents that 
achieve a percentage of air voids equal to 4% at the maximum stability value and the 
maximum specific density. This is the design content of the asphalt binder.

The stability of the test specimen is the maximum load resistance in newtons (N), that 
the compacted standard test specimen will develop at 60°C when using Marshall 
Apparatus according to MRDTM 410 (Design of Asphalt concrete Mixture Using Marshall 
Procedures). The flow value is the total deformation, in units of millimeters (mm), 
occurring in the specimen between no load and the point of maximum load during the 
stability test. 
 
3. Stability and flow Determination 
2.2- Marshall – Design Steps
 
2-HMA Design (virgin) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
                                    
                           Page 33 of 69  
Improved Hot Mix 
Asphalt Design Manual  
Kingdom of Saudi Arabia 
Ministry of Transport           
and Logistics Services 
Roads Construction Deputyship 
General Department of Quality 
and Environment  
Using Marshall Machine, stability and the flow of the specimen are evaluated as follow:  
 
1. Heat a water bath to a temperature (60 ± 1 ° C). 
2. A large enough water bath is used to absorb all samples and ensure that it is 
heated for the same period of time before testing. 
3. Measure specimens’ height 
4. Immerse specimens in water bath at 60°C±1 for 30 - 40 minutes. 
5. Prepare the testing head by cleaning the inside surface and maintain its 
temperature between 21 to 37.8 °C. Remove specimen from the water bath and dry 
the surface by towel. Place specimen in lower testing head and center, then fit 
upper testing head into position and center complete assembly in Marshall 
machine. Place flow meter over marked guide. 
6. The load gauge and flow gauge are set to 0. Apply testing load to specimen at a 
constant rate of deformation, 50±5 mm per minute, until failure occurs. The point 
of failure is defined when the maximum load reading is obtained. This maximum 
value in Newtons (N) is the Marshall Stability value and the reading on the flow 
meter at the maximum load is the flow value of the specimen. 
7. The test should be completed within half a minute (30 seconds) from the moment 
the sample is removed from the water bath. 
8. The Marshall stability is corrected for specimens with a height different from 63.5 
mm using table 15 and for modified Marshall Method stability correction use table 
16.

c. Specimen Batching and Compaction 
1. Batching 
Marshall specimens and mixture’s maximum specific gravity samples must be 
batched by aggregate component and size fraction. MOT recommends that the 
specimens be mixed individually to reduce the potential for error. Do not forget to 
add the minus No.200 size material to account.  
 
For Standard Marshall Method (AASHTO T-245), The required Marshall compacted 
specimen size is 63.5 ± 1.27 mm in height by 101.6 mm in diameter. This Method 
is applicable for HMA with NMS up to 25.0 mm. The approximate weight of 
aggregate for compacted specimen is about 1.2 Kg. Modified Marshall method 
(ASTM D5581) the specimen size is 95.2 mm in height by 152.4 mm in diameter. 
This Method is applicable for HMA with NMS more than 25.0 mm. The approximate 
weight of aggregate for compacted specimen is about 4.0 Kg  
It is generally desirable to prepare a trial specimen prior to preparing the 
aggregate batches. If the trial specimen height falls outside the height limits, the 
amount of aggregate used for the specimen should be adjusted using equation 3: 
Equation 3: 
 
𝒂𝒅𝒋. 𝒎𝒂𝒔𝒔 𝒐𝒇 𝒂𝒈𝒈𝒓𝒆𝒈𝒂𝒕𝒆= 𝟔𝟑. 𝟓 (𝟗𝟓. 𝟐) 𝒙 𝒎𝒂𝒔𝒔 𝒐𝒇 𝒖𝒔𝒆𝒅 𝒂𝒈𝒈𝒓𝒆𝒈𝒂𝒕𝒆
𝑺𝒑𝒆𝒄. 𝒉𝒆𝒊𝒈𝒉𝒕
 
 
 
The maximum specific gravity sample size of the mixture varies depending on the 
nominal maximum aggregate size of the mixture being tested. The composition of each 
Marshall compacted specimen and mixture maximum specific gravity sample is 
determined according to the following procedure: 
 
a. Determine the specimen’s PG binder content. 
b. Estimate the weight of aggregate mass required to produce compacted specimen. 
The mixture maximum specific gravity sample size is predetermined based on the 
nominal maximum aggregate size of the mixture. 
c. Determine the percentage of aggregate in the specimen from Equation 4.

e. Multiply the average percentage retained by the total mass of aggregate to 
determine the mass of each aggregate size fraction.  
f. Place the mass of each aggregate size fraction in container to determine the total 
aggregate specimen mass using a scale that meets the requirements listed in 
(Table 9). 
g. Place the container in the oven and heat to the mixing temperature. Charge the 
mixing bowl with the heated aggregate and add the required amount of binder. At 
this point, the temperature of the aggregate and the asphalt must be within the 
limits of the mixing temperatures. Do not hold asphalt binder at mixing 
temperature more than one hour. 
h. Mix the aggregate and asphalt binder (preferably with a mechanical mixer) as 
quickly and thoroughly as possible to yield a mixture having a uniform 
distribution of asphalt. 
i. Place the mixture in the oven for two hours at compaction temperature.  After two 
hours remove maximum specific gravity (Gmm) samples and allow them to 
cooldown at room temperature and Marshall specimens to be compacted.

2. Compaction 
Specimen preparation and compaction are following: 
a. Put compaction mold in oven at compaction temperature for two hours. 
Compaction mold is consisting of a base plate, forming mold and collar 
extension.  
b. After two hours, remove the mold and the plates from the oven, put the base 
plat in position in the mold, and place a paper disk on the plate. Drop the 
mixture into the mold using a funnel or other device but take care to avoid 
segregation of the mix in the mold. Then compact the asphalt mixture with a 
hot knife or hot rod (15 times) around the circumference of the mold and (15) 
times from the inside. Level the mix in the mold, place a paper disk and mold 
top plate. Place the mold in holder of the compactor. 
c. Compaction is done by Marshall Hammer following compaction parameter as 
shown in Table 19. 
d. Apply required number of blows for each side 
e. After compaction, remove the base plate and the paper disks and allow the 
specimen to cool at room temperature.

3 HMA Design (w/ Reclaimed Asphalt Pavement, RAP) 
Old paving materials usually contain a solid asphalt bond due to oxidation and also 
contain fragmented aggregate (an increase in fine materials) due to scraping or crushing 
layers. This usually requires softening the asphalt binder to achieve the targeted 
performance grade and selecting the new aggregate gradient and its properties to 
achieve the target gradient and the desired quality standards. It is also necessary to add 
a quantity of the new asphalt binder sufficient to cover the added aggregate and 
softening (modifying the properties) of the old asphalt binder. It is important to know 
how much asphalt binder is present in the RAP material, so that it can be accounted for 
in the mix design process.  Sometimes, it is also necessary to know some physical 
properties of the old asphalt binder. 
This is achieved in the following way: 
• Withdrawing a sufficient number of random samples from stockpiles or from the 
existing road to be recycled using standard methods. 
• Extraction of on the RAP to determine the asphalt binder content and properties 
of the aggregate by dissolving it in a standard solution to separate its 
components. 
• Recovery of the old asphalt binder from the solvent according to Abson method 
(AASHTO T 170) and determining its psychical properties. 
 
The overall process remains the same as for the virgin HMA design either for Superpave 
or Marshall mix design; however, extra procedures are required to accommodate the 
use of RAP. The differences include the following:  
 
a. Change in virgin binder grade may be needed depending on the amount of RAP, 
desired final binder grade, and RAP binder stiffness. 
b. The RAP aggregate is treated like another stockpile for blending and weighing. 
c. The weight of the binder in the RAP must be accounted for when batching 
aggregates. 
d. The RAP aggregate specific gravity must be estimated. 
e. The total asphalt content is reduced to compensate for the binder provided by the 
RAP. 
 
3- HMA Design (with RAP)

3.1 
Superpave System (w/RAP) 
3.1.1 Design steps for Superpave system (w/RAP) 
The process of designing HMA using RAP is the same as the virgin HMA design with the 
following additional guidelines regarding the addition of RAP. Sampling of both 
Aggregate and RAP from stockpile are similar. Obtain representative RAP samples 
according to AASHTO R 90. RAP binder content, aggregate characterization and RAP 
moisture are determined as follow: 
 
a. RAP Binder Content and Properties 
Produced HMA total binder content is consisting of virgin binder and RAP binder 
contained in the RAP. It is important to know how much asphalt binder is present 
in the RAP material, so that it can be accounted for in the mix design process. 
Determine binder content of each RAP sample using extraction method. 
Sometimes, it is also necessary to know something about the physical properties 
of the asphalt binder. In these cases, it is necessary to extract and recover the 
asphalt binder from the RAP using a solvent so that the binder can be tested.  
 
• For low RAP contents less than 10 percent, it is not necessary to do this testing 
because there is not enough of the RAP binder present to change the total 
binder properties.  
• For intermediate ranges of RAP 10 to 15 percent, the virgin binder grade can 
simply be dropped one grade.  
• For higher percentages of RAP, you will need to extract and recover the RAP 
binder and determine its properties (Appendix B) 
 
 
b. RAP Aggregate Properties (Superpave) 
RAP aggregate must meet the property requirements like virgin aggregate. The 
RAP aggregate must be analyzed to determine his gradation, specific gravity and 
consensus properties. Because the specific gravity of the RAP aggregate cannot be 
calculated directly, it is necessary to estimate it as follow:  
• Method 1 uses the extracted aggregate and separate it into coarse and 
fine fractions and individual specific gravity are determined. 
 
3.1- Superpave – Design Steps
 
3-HMA Design (with RAP)

• Method 2 uses the effective specific gravity of the RAP aggregate  Gse(RAP,Agg) 
instead of its bulk specific gravity Gsb(RAP,Agg) based on the maximum theoretical 
specific gravity of the RAP mixture Gmm(RAP) and the asphalt binder content of 
the RAP Pb(RAP) 
  
• Method 2a uses the same methodology as method 2 except that the absorption 
of the RAP aggregate Pba(RAP,agg)  is assumed, and the bulk specific gravity 
Gsb(RAP,Agg) is calculated. 
 
It is recommended to use either method 2 or 2a. 
 
c. Moisture in RAP 
Usually, RAP is dried When batching samples in laboratory, but when used on site, 
some moisture may remain within the RAP. When determining the weight of the 
batch at the asphalt plant, the amount of moisture in the RAP must be taken into 
account. If the amount of moisture is not calculated, the actual weight of the old 
RAP added will be less than required because part of the weight will be moisture, 
rather than the net weight of the RAP. The moisture content in the RAP is calculated 
as follows:

3.1.2 Superpave Specimen Formulation (w/RAP) 
 
This section outlines the procedure for batching and compaction of recycled mixture test 
specimens according to AASHTO T 312 and AASHTO R 30. 
 
a. Aggregate and RAP Preparation (Superpave) 
Obtain representative aggregate and RAP samples according to AASHTO R 90. The 
RAP aggregate is treated like another stockpile for blending and weighing. The RAP 
must be heated to make it workable and to mix it with the virgin materials Avoid 
heating the RAP more than one time. Once a RAP sample has been heated to mixing 
temperature, it must be used within one hour. It’s better to separate RAP into 
Coarse and fine fractions by splitting on a 4.75mm sieve. 
 
 
b. Specimens Batching and Compaction (Superpave) 
The process remains the same as for the virgin HMA design (Superpave), except 
that: 
 
a. Do not extract the RAP binder from the RAP aggregate 
 
b. Add the RAP as the last aggregate component prior to adding the virgin binder 
 
c. It is important to remember that part of the weight of the RAP is binder and the 
total asphalt content has to be reduced to compensate for the binder provided 
by the RAP 
 
d. When batching the RAP, the weight of the RAP will include both aggregate and 
binder. It is necessary to increase the weight of RAP and decrease the amount 
of new binder added to take the presence of this RAP binder into account. The 
weight of dry RAP that would provide a given weight of RAP aggregate is 
calculated as: 
Equation 8: 
𝑀𝑑𝑟𝑦𝑅𝐴𝑃=
𝑀𝑅𝐴𝑃𝐴𝑔𝑔
100 −𝑃𝑏(𝑅𝐴𝑃)
∗100

For previous equation clarification, consider the following example: The coarse fraction 
of RAP retained on 4.75mm sieve is 60 % of the RAP with 6.0 % of binder content and the 
fine fraction of RAP passing 4.75mm sieve is 40 % of the RAP with 4.0 % of binder 
content.  The batch of aggregate for a mix design is 4000 g with trial blend of 25% of 
RAP. 
 
• For a 4000g aggregate batch, we have 25% of RAP = 1000 g of RAP 
 
• 60% the RAP is retained on sieve 4.75mm and 40% is passing. Therefore, we need 
60% of 1000 g (600g) of coarse RAP aggregate and 40 % of 1000 g (400g) of fine 
RAP aggregate

3.2 
Marshall System (w/RAP) 
3.2.1 Design steps for Marshall System (w/RAP) 
The process of designing HMA using RAP is the same as the virgin HMA design with the 
following additional guidelines regarding the addition of RAP. Sampling of both 
Aggregate and RAP from stockpile are similar. Obtain representative RAP samples 
according to AASHTO R 90. RAP binder content and aggregate characterization are as 
follow: 
 
a. RAP Binder Content and Properties 
Produced HMA total binder content is consisting of virgin binder and RAP binder 
contained in the RAP. It is important to know how much asphalt binder is present 
in the RAP material, so that it can be accounted for in the mix design process. 
Determine binder content of each RAP sample using extraction method. 
Sometimes, it is also necessary to know something about the physical properties 
of the asphalt binder. In these cases, it is necessary to extract and recover the 
asphalt binder from the RAP using a solvent so that the binder can be tested.  
 
• For low RAP contents less than 10 percent, it is not necessary to do this testing 
because there is not enough of the RAP binder present to change the total 
binder properties.  
• For intermediate ranges of RAP 10 to 15 percent, the virgin binder grade can 
simply be dropped one grade.  
• For higher percentages of RAP, you will need to extract and recover the RAP 
binder and determine its properties (Appendix B)

b. RAP Aggregate Properties (Marshall) 
RAP aggregate must meet the property requirements like virgin aggregate. The 
RAP aggregate must be analyzed to determine his gradation, specific gravity and 
the quality requirements of MOT Standard Specifications. Because the specific 
gravity of the RAP aggregate cannot be calculated directly, it is necessary to 
estimate it as follow:  
• Method 1 uses the extracted aggregate and separate it into coarse and 
fine fractions and individual specific gravity are determined. 
• Method 2 uses the effective specific gravity of the RAP aggregate  Gse(RAP,Agg) 
instead of its bulk specific gravity Gsb(RAP,Agg) based on the maximum theoretical 
specific gravity of the RAP mixture Gmm(RAP) and the asphalt binder content of 
the RAP Pb(RAP) 
• Method 2a uses the same methodology as method 2 except that the absorption 
of the RAP aggregate Pba(RAP,agg)  is assumed, and the bulk specific gravity 
Gsb(RAP,Agg) is calculated. 
It is recommended to use either method 2 or 2a. 
c. Moisture in RAP 
Usually, RAP is dried When batching samples in laboratory, but when used on site, 
some moisture may remain within the RAP. When determining the weight of the 
batch at the asphalt plant, the amount of moisture in the RAP must be taken into 
account. If the amount of moisture is not calculated, the actual weight of the old 
RAP added will be less than required because part of the weight will be moisture, 
rather than the net weight of the RAP. The moisture content in the RAP is calculated 
as follows:  
Equation 9: 
 
  
    %𝑀𝑜𝑖𝑠𝑡𝑢𝑟𝑒=
𝑊𝑤−𝑊𝑑
𝑊𝑑
𝑋100 
Where: 
Ww: Mass of wet RAP 
Wd : Mass of RAP after drying to constant mass  
 
Sometimes you need to know how much RAP with moisture to weigh out to provide 
a certain dry mass of RAP. This can be calculated as follows: 
 Equation 10: 
𝑊𝑤= 𝑊𝑑(1 + %𝑀𝑜𝑖𝑠𝑡𝑢𝑟𝑒)

3.2.2 Marshall Specimen Formulation (w/RAP) 
 
a. Aggregate and RAP Preparation (Marshall) 
Obtain representative aggregate and RAP samples according to AASHTO R 90. The 
RAP aggregate is treated like another stockpile for blending and weighing. The RAP 
must be heated to make it workable and to mix it with the virgin materials Avoid 
heating the RAP more than one time. Once a RAP sample has been heated to mixing 
temperature, it must be used within one hour. It’s better to separate RAP into 
Coarse and fine fractions by splitting on a 4.75mm sieve. 
 
b. Specimens Batching and Compaction (Marshall) 
The process remains the same as for the virgin HMA design (Marshall), except that: 
 
a. Do not extract the RAP binder from the RAP aggregate 
 
b. Add the RAP as the last aggregate component prior to adding the virgin binder 
 
c. It is important to remember that part of the weight of the RAP is binder and the 
total asphalt content has to be reduced to compensate for the binder provided by 
the RAP 
 
d. When batching the RAP, the weight of the RAP will include both aggregate and 
binder. It is necessary to increase the weight of RAP and decrease the amount 
of new binder added to take the presence of this RAP binder into account. The 
weight of dry RAP that would provide a given weight of RAP aggregate is 
calculated as: 
 
Equation 11: 
MdryRAP =
MRAPAgg
100 −Pb(RAP)
∗100 
 
where: 
      𝑴𝒅𝒓𝒚𝑹𝑨𝑷: 
Mass of dry RAP, (g) 
𝑴𝑹𝑨𝑷𝑨𝒈𝒈: 
Mass of RAP aggregate, (g) 
𝑷𝒃(𝑹𝑨𝑷): 
RAP binder content. (%)

4 HMA Design Verification (Superpave / Marshall) 
 
The MOT will verify HMA designs as needed. The submitted HMA design has to be coded 
as shown in appendix C. Verification may include a review of the submitted HMA designs 
and performing tests on collected plant samples (One-point check) as well. This process 
will be accomplished within 30 days from the date of design submittal to MOT for review, 
verification and approval. Approval of HMA design by the MOT does not relieve the 
contractor of his obligation to produce bituminous concrete mixtures conforming to all 
specified requirements  in all stages of the project / work. Verification and approval 
process involve the following: 
 
• HMA Design Review (Superpave / Marshall) 
• One-Point Check (Superpave / Marshall) 
 
 
4.1 
HMA Design Review (Superpave / Marshall) 
MOT will perform necessary review for submitted HMA design to check conformance 
with specifications and criteria. Based on this review, one of the following actions will be 
issued:  
 
a. HMA design is accepted  
 
b. HMA design is accepted with comments (corrective actions are needed) 
 
c. HMA design is not accepted for not meeting specifications and project requirements.  
 
In case of “a” and “b” above, the MOT may request (if necessary) plant aggregate, PG, 
and HMA samples for one-point check as illustrated next. In case of “c”. the design has 
to be revised by the supplier (contractor/supervision) and re-submitted to MOT for 
approval.

4.2 
One-Point Check (Superpave / Marshall) 
The MOT may request (if necessary) plant aggregate, PG, and HMA samples for one-
point. The MOT may also have laboratory HMA prepared and tested to verify the design 
prior to plant production (one-point) verification. MOT may ask or itself collect plant 
samples including:  
 
• 
Hot bins aggregate samples. Each fraction of the aggregate size (50 Kg) shall be 
placed in a substantial, sealed container separately and properly labeled 
 
• 
Eight liters of PG binder. The PG binder shall be in clean, sealed containers 
suitable for heating and properly labeled 
 
• 
HMA samples (minimum 100 Kg) produced at the project plant  
Based on obtained results, one of the following final decisions will be issued by MOT:  
a. HMA design is approved  
b. HMA design is approved with comments (few results deviate slightly from 
specification and project requirements. The Supplier/contractor/supervision will be 
directed to take corrective actions (It may not be necessary to submit the design) 
c. HMA design is rejected (results showed high deviations from design limits, 
specifications and project requirements). The supplier/contractor/supervision will 
be directed to make necessary adjustment and re-submit the HMA design for review, 
verification and approval.  
 
In case of “a” and “b” above, the contractor/supervision must construct a minimum 200-
meter-long field control strip as explained next.

4.3 
Field Test Strip (Superpave / Marshall) 
If the submitted HMA design is approved, the MOT directs contractor/supervision to 
construct field control strip with the complete available paving width (lanes and 
shoulders). The strip will be evaluated for its constructability and compatibility. HMA 
samples will be tested to check conformance with design Job Mix Formula (JMF). 
Production tolerances for Superpave and Marshall mixes are listed in Table 20 and Table 
21, respectively.  
 
Evaluation of the test strip is the responsibility of supervision team. Copy of test-strip 
results maybe requested by MOT. Test section shall prove acceptable results and 
construction performance in order to proceed with production and paving. If test section 
proved unsatisfactorily, corrective actions shall be made by contractor in order to bring 
used materials/HMA production methods/construction equipment and techniques to 
comply with specification. Paving shall not be permitted till a successful test strip is 
achieved.

5 Polymer Modified Bitumen (PMB)  
 
a. Neat Asphalt Binder (NAB): consists of the asphalt binder that is directly produced 
from petroleum refineries owned by the Saudi Aramco. Currently, Saudi Aramco 
grades this asphalt binder as penetration grade 60/70; while, in Superpave grading 
system this type was graded to be of PG 64S-10. Therefore, this type can only be 
used without modification in the projects and pavements that require PG of 64S-10 
in accordance to the Superpave mix design requirements. 
 
b. Polymer Modified Binder (PMB): consists of bitumen blended with a synthetic 
polymer or crumb rubber. PMBs are used to enhance the performance of binders on 
heavily trafficked or distressed pavement surfaces, often in adverse climatic 
conditions. Property improvements include reduced temperature susceptibility, 
increased elasticity or resilience, increased cohesion and improved tenacity once a 
bond has been established. This leads to improve performance include lower risk of 
bleeding, improved crack resistance, better aggregate retention and less 
deformation at high temperatures. Polymer groups are as follows: 
 
• 
Elastomeric polymers including styrene-butadiene-styrene (SBS), styrene-
butadiene rubber (SBR) and polybutadiene (PBD). Binders modified with 
elastomeric polymer have improved resilience or elasticity, are less temperature 
susceptible. 
 
• 
Plastomeric polymers including ethylene vinyl acetate (EVA), ethylene 
methacrylate (EMA), atactic polypropylene (APP), and polypropylene (PE). Binders 
modified with plastomeric polymer have increased stiffness. 
 
• 
Crumb rubber is generally obtained from shredding and grinding of scrap rubber 
from vehicle tires. When blended with bitumen the rubber behaves as a form of 
elastomer 
 
The Superpave system uses a PG asphalt binder specification with a matching set of 
tests. The system for specifying asphalt binders is a performance-based specification. 
It specifies binders on the basis of the climate and attendant pavement temperatures in 
which the binder is expected to serve. Physical property requirements remain the same, 
5- Polymer Modified Bitumen (PMB)
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
                                    
                           Page 54 of 69  
Improved Hot Mix 
Asphalt Design Manual  
Kingdom of Saudi Arabia 
Ministry of Transport           
and Logistics Services 
Roads Construction Deputyship 
General Department of Quality 
and Environment  
but the temperature at which the binder must attain the properties changes. In 
Superpave, binders are graded such as PG 64S-10. The first number, 64, is often called 
the "high temperature grade”. This means that the binder would possess adequate 
physical properties up to max. 64°C. This would be the high pavement temperature 
corresponding to the climate in which the binder is actually expected to serve. This 
temperature is derived from the highest average 7-day air temperature ever recorded 
near the project site. Likewise, the second number, (-10), is often called the "low 
temperature grade" and means that the binder would possess adequate physical 
properties in pavements down to max. -10°C. 
 
In PG grading, additional consideration is given to the type of loading (open highway, city 
streets, intersections, etc.). The “S” letter refers to the standard traffic level lower than 
10 million equivalent single axle loads (ESALs) with the traffic speed more than the 
standard traffic speed of 70 km/h. The asphalt binder materials that are required for the 
construction and maintenance of the roads in the Kingdom Of Saudi Arabia can be either 
Neat Asphalt Binder (NAB), which is unmodified, or Polymer Modified Binder (PMB); and 
in both cases, the asphalt binder must meet the performance-based specifications 
presented in AASHTO M332 and summarized in Table 22.

5.1 
PMB Quality Control Plan 
The Producer of a PMB shall provide and maintain a detailed Quality Control Plan. The 
producer has the option to copy information from the specifications should they believe 
it will provide their personnel with necessary information. The producer shall submit the 
QC Plan to the MOT for approval and shall not start work without an approved QC Plan. 
The approval process for the producer’s QC Plan may include inspection of QC testing 
equipment, sampling and testing demonstration by the QC technician(s) and testing of 
proficiency samples to assure an acceptable level of performance. 
 
Approval of the QC Plan will be based on the inclusion of the required information and 
does not imply any warranty by the Ministry that the QC Plan will result in production 
that complies with the specifications. It remains the responsibility of the producer to 
accomplish such compliance. QC plan shall include, as a minimum, the following 
positions, and qualifications. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
The PMB Producer is responsible to ensure that the PMB is produced following the 
polymer supplier/manufacturer’s recommendations as well as meeting the 
specifications of the MOT. The PMB producer must make sure all the equipment needed 
for the PMB production and testing is in a good condition and calibrated up to date.

and condition will never be a probability.

5.3 
PMB Production, Storage and Hauling  
PMB blending, agitation, storage and hauling shall include the following precautions, in 
addition to MOT specifications and manufacturer’s guidelines: 
1. PMB shall be produced in automatic mode following the manufacturer’s 
recommendations and specifications.  
2. High shear mill shall be appropriately used in the initial mixing phase 
3. PMB shall be agitated for appropriate period (based on polymer type and 
specifications)  
4. PMB shall be stored in heat-insulated tanks with proper heating and circulation 
system. Tanks must be provided with thermometers located in well-visible 
points. The temperature of the PMB should not be deviated from the storage fixed 
temperature in more than ten degrees Celsius (± 10). 
5. Different PMB grades are stored in separate tanks  
6. If a test result indicates non-compliance of any shipment with the specifications, 
the producer shall identify the material; cease additional shipment until material 
is brought back to specification.

23 presents the QC testing procedures. Test frequencies shall be performed following the 
MOT specifications.

14. Load number, Amount of PGB in vehicle  
15. Cumulative PGB daily total, ton 
16. PGB time of arrival at jobsite, PGB time of discharge at jobsite                    
17. Temperature of PGB when discharge 
18. Recommended mixing and compaction temperature at project 
19. Registration number of deliver vehicle 
20. Driver's name or number  
 
All test results and production data shall be properly documented at the PMB production 
facility location. Control charts shall be maintained. Every PMB delivery load shall 
include producer certificate of compliance with specification. Certificate must show lot 
number and test results.

Specific Gravity Determination 
Determine the specific gravity of aggregate as per AASHTO T 84, AASHTO T 85, ASTM C 
127, and ASTM C 128.    
 
Composite Aggregate Bulk and Apparent Specific Gravity 
The bulk and apparent specific gravities for the total aggregate are calculated as follows: 
𝐺𝑠𝑏𝑜𝑟 𝐺𝑠𝑎= [ 𝑃1 + 𝑃2 + ⋯+ 𝑃𝑛
𝑃1
𝐺1 + 𝑃2
𝐺2 + ⋯+ 𝑃𝑛
𝐺𝑛
] 
Where: 
Gsb: 
Bulk specific gravity for the total aggregate, reported to the nearest 0.001, 
Gsa: 
Apparent specific gravity for the total aggregate, 
 Pn: 
% of individual aggregate components based on total mass of aggregate, 
Gn: 
Bulk or apparent specific gravities of aggregates. 
 
Since the bulk specific gravity of mineral filler is difficult to determine, the apparent 
specific gravity is used instead.

P: 
Total loose mixture, percent by total mass of mixture = 100 percent 
Gmm: Maximum specific gravity of hot mixture asphalt, AASHTO T 209 & ASTM D204 
Gb: 
Specific gravity of PG binder at 25ºC. 
Pb: 
The percentage of asphalt binder in the total mass of the mixture

Appendix B: RAP Characterization  
For low content of RAP (≤ 15% by total HMA weight), no RAP characterization is needed. 
For high percentages of RAP over 15%, you will need to extract and recover the RAP 
binder and determine its properties to construct a blending chart. The RAP binder has to 
be extracted and then recovered for testing. A solvent extraction must be used when 
recovering the RAP binder. 
 
a) Superpave and Marshall System 
The physical properties of the recovered RAP binder and the desired final binder grade 
are needed for constructing of the blending chart. The extracted and recovered RAP 
binder must be tested in the dynamic shear rheometer (DSR) at a high temperature as if 
it was original, unaged binder. Based on early results Figures B-1 and B-2 were 
developed for RAP content versus PMB high temperatures for recovered binder grade of 
PG≤ 82 and PG > 82 oC, respectively. According to RAP content (% by total HMA weight), 
those figures may be used as guidance to evaluate the minimum virgin PMB grade 
required to achieve (after mixing with RAP) the project target PG grade. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Figure B-1 Recovered Bitumen from RAP High temperature, T ˂ 82 oC 
(G*/sinδ ≥ 1.0 Kpa)
